## Page 20 – Brand Extension Summary, House of Brands, Shadow Endorser

### Summary: Brand Extensions

**5 implications of extensions:**
Good, more good, bad, ugly, more ugly

**Pros of brand extensions:**
Known name, easy recognition, favourable associations rub off

**Cons of brand extensions:**
Parent comes with a baggage, it is not cheaper

**What product category to stretch into?**
Based on 6 criteria:
i) Market attractiveness
ii) Brand value consistency
iii) Organizational strengths
iv) Internal-external fit
v) Customers
vi) Managing 4Ps

Check brand value consistency (item ii) with customers – is hair oil close to shampoo?

---

### Summary: More on Extensions

**In India, adverse impact of extension failure on parent doesn't seem to be high**

**Three classifications of extensions:**
- Line (same product) vs Brand (different product)
- Product related (Cinthol soap), Image related (talc), Unrelated (TV)
- Vertical (different prices) vs Horizontal (different products)

Formula brands difficult to stretch, philosophy brands easy.

**Paradox of brand extensions:**
If the parent is too strong or too weak it cannot be stretched.

**Product related extensions:**
i) How many variants in product related extensions?
ii) How many do you think will customers remember?

---

### Summary: Cannibalization and Unrelated Extensions

ii) **What to do about cannibalization?**
   Design for 20% cannibalization

iii) **Upward or downward extension?**
   What is the "word" the parent owns is key

**Unrelated extensions:**
i) Unrelated extensions are possible in philosophy brands
   Question is, how many extensions (GE? Gucci?)
   Bigger question, will they make money?
ii) Unrelated extensions sit best on organizational or family names

---

### House of Brands

House of brands is in 2 types – i) unconnected ii) shadow endorser

**Unconnected:**
i) Natraj and Apsara unconnected to Hind Pencils
ii) Reckitt Benckiser's brands Dettol, Moov and Cherry Blossom do not mention it in ads
iii) Volkswagen India doesn't mention Audi
- Give an example from India?
- What is the plus of this strategy? **It is less risky – conservative branding**

**Not connected:** Parent doesn't want customer to know. Prefer you not to know the connect.

**Shadow endorser:** Parent doesn't tell you, but you get to know. Company doesn't mind if you know the connect.

---

### Shadow Endorser Examples

**House of brands:**
- JLR and Tata, Yardley and Wipro
- https://wiproconsumercare.com/brands-india/
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6iBYerifYoo
- Yardley London Daily Wear Perfumes | Kriti Sanon | Make an Impression Naturally
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rLtFIrqhfng
- Jaguar | Copy Nothing
- What is interesting about the ad? **Shah Rukh Lux ad – controversy is good!**
- Forget Tatas, even the car is not there in the ad
- Why is the Tata name not there on JLR?
- Sony owned Aiwa, Nokia owned Vertu
- We know Sonata is a Titan brand / They never mention it, it is understood

---

### Token Endorser

**One reason why the article is wrong when applied to India?**
Token endorser – Aditya Birla Fashion

Token endorser is never center stage (P13)
(So Aditya Birla appears discreetly after the product ad)
Endorser (Aditya Birla) already well known (P13)
Consistently presented (after the ad – P13)

- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=V3I-R-QdTjY
- Flower Bomb: Spring-Summer '24 | W for Woman
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FjIXZim-K5M
- Dive into a world where every moment is a celebration with Aurelia

**Shadow endorser** = implicit endorsement
**Token endorser** = explicit endorsement

---

### Token Endorsement – After Every Brand Ad

- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HQGfqhPZWVg – Whisper [2]
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ys-125an3qA – Pantene [3]
- In the past P&G India and HUL were like this, not now
- Give an example of token endorser in India?

**Linked Name:**
- McAloo Tikki
- FeviKwik = Fevicol + quick adhesive
- Nimeasy (dish cleaner), Nimwash (wash vegetables), Nimyle (floor cleaner) – ITC

---

### Strong Endorser Examples

- Ethnix from Raymond
- Kuhl fans from the house of Kent
- Irth, house of Titan
- Sonata from Tata
- Vivanta from Taj
- Starbucks, a Tata alliance
- Skinn by Titan
- Tanishq, a Tata product
- Ginger, a Tata enterprise

- Taneira, a Tata product
- Mia by Tanishq

**Food for thought:** Tatas seem to have a pronounced liking for the "strong endorser"

---

### Co-Driver vs Master Brand as Driver

**How is "co-driver" different from "Master brand as driver"?**
- In co-driver both master and sub-brand important
- In second case master brand is the driver
- Co-driver: Godrej No.1 (https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QJHSfpCl12Y4 [voice, visual: -20])

**Master sub brand** – Parent brand as driver, in which categories?
- In music systems, TVs, why?
- Attribute is branded, it can become irrelevant
- Onida KY Thunder, Onida Candy
- LG Golden Eye, Sony Triluminos

---

### Branded House

- LG appliances and electronics – functional and easy
- Point to ponder: Is the basis, identity, positioning or value proposition?

**Branded house (same identity):**
- Tata steel – what is its value prop? Premium, Centrum, Astrum, Steelium
- Tata Tea – what is its value prop? Popular, pricing to beat Unilever

- Corporate brand dominance → Branded house
- Product brand dominance → House of brands

**Any recent radical changes in brand architecture in India?**

## Page 21 – Brand Hierarchy Tree, Portfolio Structure, Tata Brand Roles

### Brand Hierarchy Tree for Colgate Oral Care Products

A tree diagram showing Colgate's brand hierarchy:

**Root (top):** Colgate

**Second level (5 branches):**
- Colgate Toothpaste
- Colgate Toothbrush
- Colgate Dental Floss
- Colgate Mouthrinse
- Colgate Fluoride Tablets

**Third level (under Colgate Toothpaste, 4 variants):**
- Plus
- Tartar Control (Tartar?)
- Classic
- Youth
- Color Change

**Fourth level (further sub-variants shown):**
- Diamond Head
- "The Wild Ones"

---

### Brand Portfolio Structure

**Brand groupings means?**
- How can the brands be grouped together?
- How many segments are my brands covering?

**Why should we examine brand groupings?**
- Will tell you what opportunities you are covering across products
- By prices (Harrier – hp, Tiago – affordable)
- By product (cars, multi-utility vehicles, cross-overs)
- By quality (designer/premium)
- By design (classic – Safari, contemporary – Altroz)

**Brand groupings example: Vini Cosmetics (Darshan Patel – read about him, Krack, Moov)**
Vini divides its portfolio into 3 types of products:
i) Look good (powders – White Tone face powder)
ii) Do good (anti-ageing for 40+ – Prepair4050)
iii) Smell good (deos – Fogg)

---

### Tata Brand Portfolio Roles (Table)

A table mapping brand types to Tata brand examples across three time periods:

| Type | Brand day before | Brand yesterday | Brand today |
|---|---|---|---|
| Silver bullet (fame, nursery) | Jaguar, Magic | Jaguar | Tigor |
| Linchpin brand (initial, school) | Indica | Indigo | Hexa (1600 pm) |
| Strategic brand (growth, college) | Ace | Indica | Punch, Nexon |
| Cash cow (late, maturity, job) | Ace (LCV), Magic (covered top) | Ace, Jaguar? | Ace, Jaguar? |

---

### Summary: Brand Relationship Spectrum

9 types of relationships between the parent and the brand – from house of brands to branded house:

i) **House of brands (unconnected)**
   Parent doesn't want the customer to know the connect
   Reckitt and its brands Cherry Blossom, Moov, Dettol

ii) **House of brands (shadow endorser)**
   Parent doesn't tell customer, customer gets to know, that is OK
   Implicit endorsement
   Titan and Sonata (Titan not mentioned, OK if the customer knows)

iii) **Token endorser**
   Explicit endorsement, though faint
   Appears discreetly at the end of the ad

iv) **Linked Name**
   Compound name of parent and brand
   McAloo Tikki

v) **Strong endorser**
   Parent seen in conjunction with brand, though at some distance
   Ethnix by Raymond

vi, vii) **Sub brands**
   Parent and brand seen next to each other
   - Co-driver – Parent = brand (Godrej No.1)
   - Master brand as driver – Parent > brand (Music systems)
   - Brand as driver – Brand > Parent (Indica?)

viii, ix) **Branded house**
   Parent = brand name
   - Same identity – all products have same value proposition (LG)
   - Different identity – different products have different value propositions (Tata)

---

## Page 22 – Brand Portfolio Summary, Three Silos of Corporate Brand, Product vs Corporate Brand

### Summary: Brand Portfolio (4 Elements)

**4 elements:**
i) Brand rel. with parent – Product market context roles (spectrum)
ii) Brand rel. with siblings – Brand portfolio structure
iii) Brand rel. with itself – Portfolio graphics
iv) Brand portfolio roles – is this architecture profitable?

Brand relationship spectrum is a subset of brand architecture.
i) and iii) already covered.

**Brand portfolio structure – Brand relationship with siblings – 3 components:**

a) **Brand range** (similar to product scope)
   How far the brand can extend without encroaching on siblings?
   Nexon? Tata Nexon? New brand name?

b) **Brand hierarchy trees**
   Family tree of the parent, brand and siblings (Tata or Colgate tree)

c) **Brand groups**
   How many opportunities did the brand and siblings exhaust?
   Vini cosmetics – Look good, Do good, Smell good
   Pepsi – Fun for you, Good for you, Better for you

**Brand portfolio roles – Is the architecture profitable?**
- Silver bullet – brings fame – Java for Sun
- Linchpin – sales tomorrow, profit tomorrow – Benz self driving trucks
- Strategic – sales today, profit tomorrow – EV brands for car cos.
- Cash cow – sales today, profit today – Lorries for Tatas

---

### Three Silos of Corporate Brand

A table showing three distinct silos:

| | **Silo 1 – Identity** | **Silo 2 – Comm.** | **Silo 3 – Audience** |
|---|---|---|---|
| Content | Corp mission, philosophy, etc. | Communication, Employee views, Products & services | Customers, Government, Banks, suppliers etc |
| Summary | What we are | What we say | What they think of us |
| | Corporate Group | Communication | Customers and other stakeholders |
| | Input | Process | Output |

---

### Product Brand vs Corporate Brand (Comparison Table)

A table comparing product brands vs corporate brands:

| Subject | Product Brand | Corporate Brand |
|---|---|---|
| Nature | Tangible; Can be Experienced? | Intangible |
| Focus attention on | The product | The company |
| Driven by | Middle Management? | Top Management |
| Target Audience | Customers | Multiple stakeholders |
| Delivered by | Marketing / Sales Dept | Whole company |
| Communication Mix | Marketing communication | Integrated corporate communication (Internal / External) |
| Time Horizon | Short (Life of the product)? / Functional? | Long (Life of the company) / Strategic |

---

### Inputs: Corporate Philosophy

- Corporate brand is an expression of corporate strategic intent (Urde, 1999)
- Gillette wanted to be technology leader
- Good corporate philosophy grabs the soul of its employees (Collins & Porras, 1991)
- Corporate philosophy is different from goals which are tactical and SMART (?)
- Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Relevant and Timebound

**The Tata Perspective:**
- More Indians are suffering from lack of opportunities than lack of food – JRD
- Indians are capable of delivering great results given an opportunity
- In Sweden airport staff used to set their watches to Indian Airlines flight landing
- JRD himself used to check the brightness of spoons, how hostesses smiled
- Fredrick Upcott – What? Indians making steel? (Creation of Wealth – R. M. Lala)
- What are core values?

---

### The Core Values & Corporate Do's and Don'ts

**Core values result in Corporate Do's and Don'ts:**

**Don'ts:**
- Tatas may not invest in liquor even if it makes money
- ITC though in smoking, may not show women smoking

**Dos:**
- Tata group's recognition of innovation – "Best failed idea" contest
- Tata's values – We believe in ethics ("newspaper copy test")
- Pro – Ratan Tata: I know why we lost the Singapore airlines contract
- Con – Radio tapes showed all

**Two sources worth checking on corporate governance:**
i) https://www.ingovern.com/post/nifty-next-50-resoluions-2023-ingovern-recomm/mangelions
ii) https://www.moneville.in/

## Page 23 – Corporate Culture, Tata Product Communication, Employee Views, Financial Community

### Corporate Culture?

Corp culture for an agile organization follows 3 laws (Dunning, 2018):
i) Law of the small team
ii) Law of the customer
iii) Law of the network

**You are an outsider, how do you infer culture of a company?**
Go by what they do, not what they say:

a) Narayana Murthy – paying for wife, process for resolution, beautifying building, one of the directors fined, Gold standard of guidance, on NASDAQ not for money

b) Multinationals – do they buy property in India or lease?
"Against all odds, the IT story of India" – Kris Gopalakrishnan et. al., 2022

c) Is there a tangible indicator that can signal e.g. integrity?
- How clean are their accounts?
- 40% of Indian companies' accounts are suspect (Saurabh Mukherjea)
- How do you check them? Forensic accounting, get some CAs, CFAs trained in this…

---

### Product Communication – What Do You Think of Their Product Comm.?

Given the diffuse nature of the Tata group:
- A centralized corporate biased communication was inevitable
- Traditionally corporate identity was diffuse across Tata group companies
- Naturally because the nature of the products, positioning, history
- Tata Taj – subdued, hard selling doesn't work in premium products/services
- Tata tea – aggressive, because the domain is very competitive

Under Ratan Tata the rainbow of products was pushed into corp dominant arch.
Basically, to signal individual company CEOs that the boss is Bombay House!
Move from product and corp dominant arch is in fact HQ trying to assert itself.

**Conclusions:**
i) Products and services need domain specific communication (high or low decibel)
ii) A corporate needs to have a semblance of centralization in messaging
iii) What appears as product vs corporate communication might be organizational politics

---

### Employees View – How Do You Think They Rate the Group?

Employees engage at 4 levels (intellectual, social, affective and organizational).
Affective engagement means employees getting energized because of work content.
Unless employees trust the corporate brand, customers won't (Yaniv and Farkas, 2005).

How is the engagement in Tatas? Different at different levels.
It appears social and organizational engagement is higher than intellectual & affective.

**Top rung – which side are you on?**
JRD time vs Ratan's time
Satraps vs tamed lions:
- Darbari Seth, Kerkar (hotels), T'walla (Voltas), R. Modi (Tata steel), P'vala (ACC)
- Especially the last two
- They ran their companies like their empires under benign gaze of JRD Tata
- But Ratan Tata wanted to tame all satraps, become the boss, and he did!
- Therefore, at different levels employees have different views on Tata empire

---

### Products/Services – How Do You Think Tata Group Rates on This?

What is common to products/services they will enter in future?
a) Technology barrier – exited soaps (TOMCO – Hamam)
b) Investment barrier – Not many Cos can invest billions in takeovers (Corus)

Wide variety – Steel, auto, IT, salt, drilling, engineering, finance, etc.
A behemoth with several product and service capabilities.
How are they faring in different product categories?
In leading products and services – middling, sometimes struggling.

---

### Tata Group Recent Developments

R. Jagannathan, Swarajya – when C. Mistry was booted, only 2 Tata cos were in profits.
Tata – a great brand in search of good enough products, what day feet?

**Now – all products and services are turning around:**
- Tata Steel, Tata Motors, Tata Power
- Combined market value of Tata's listed affiliates shot up from $140bn (2017) to $400bn in 2024
- The group's net debt to income ratio fell from eight in 2020 to just 2.4 [27]
- Cars getting more desirable
- New superapp Neu (for Tata group shopping and payments)

**What are the 6 big, new initiatives of Tata group?**
i) Personal care – Studio West (part of Westside), Skinn (part of Titan)
ii) A payment app that competes with Gpay, Phonepe (for all payments)
iii) Qmin – Indian Hotels' home food delivery, food trucks for on-the-go meals
iv) Semi conductor chip manufacturing application to GoI
v) Healthcare – 1 mg, online doctor consultation, medical devices
vi) Edtech – Online education for Class 1 to X [22]
Btw don't forget the 470 aircraft (!) ordered by Air India

---

### Consumers – How Do They Rate the Tata Group?

Consumers rate different products differently.
Presence in multiple categories gives confidence (recollect brand extension).
Yet, literature on umbrella brands says that quality variations…
…across product categories leads to loss of confidence in the parent brand.
High variance in delivery inevitable given the range of products/services.
That is how conglomerates concede share to competitors.
Tata steel yard and Tata mobile connection.

**Financial community? (Corp conduct vs stock price)**
Weak correlation globally between corp good behaviour and stock price (Brammer et al. 2009), (Gok & Ozkaya, 2011).
Similar results are seen in India.
Financial analysts respect the Tata group, but they want performance.
Each Tata company is rated purely based on its own results, not the group's.
Sometime back when Tata Motors domestic business was not doing well…
…all that analysts were worried about was JLR sales (>4000?)

---

### How Do They Treat Minority Shareholders?

The TVS and Murugappa group have settled family disputes in such a way…
…that the listed companies are not impacted.
Therefore, minority shareholders are not impacted by family disputes [24].
Contrast this with Subhas Chandra of Zee TV and his group.
Brilliant entrepreneur and a ………… [25].

**Suppliers – How Do They Rate the Group?**
Corporate (OEM) reputation matters for suppliers, if… (Flax et al., 2016):
i) The OEM is ethical and candid in its relationships
ii) The supplier is strategically integrated with OEM

The Indian story is a partial confirmation.
No supplier is ever happy in India with a big group to which he supplies.
He is at their mercy.
Tatas have centralized buying – can you bargain with them for tyre price?
It means one lakh tyres less if they take business elsewhere – do you afford it?

---

### Influential Groups – How Do They Rate the Group?

Civil society intuitively suspects corporate groups.
Corporate groups often use CSR to (Hamann & Acutt, 2003):
i) accommodate (make cosmetic changes to look socially acceptable)
ii) legitimisation (influence public discourse to make corp actions acceptable)
Civil society should engage in 'critical cooperation' not obstructionism.

**Criticism – Arundhati Roy (Capitalism – a ghost story) vs Aakar Patel:**
AR – "We all watch Tata Sky, we surf the net with Tata Photon, we ride in Tata taxis, we stay in Tata Hotels, we eat in Tata bone china and stir it with teaspoons made of Tata Steel. We buy Tata books in Tata bookshops. *Hum Tata ka namak khate hain.* We're under siege."

---

### Media – The Ascent

When adverse media coverage hits a firm it should hit back digitally (Fan et al., 2013).
Toyota's positive media coverage, twice as effective as adverse media coverage…
…when it had to recall millions of cars.

**Tata group and the media:**
By and large good, despite Nira Radia.
Contrast this with Reliance.
Most Indian media is scared of Mukesh Ambani, why?
He owns it (e.g. CNN-IBN).
The Economist is not afraid – "The unloved billionaire", 2 Aug 2014.
Economist – "This secretive and politically powerful private empire is not a national champion but an embarrassment".
Tatas by contrast are viewed favorably, by and large.
Tatas are respected, Ambanis are feared.

---

### Tata – Summary Table (Silos)

| Item | Silo 1 – Identity (Corp mission, etc.) | Silo 2 – Comm. (Mark. Comm., emp. views, prods) | Silo 3 – Audience (Stake holders) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Summary | Tempered aggression unlike Reliance | Unified vision under Ratan Tata; consolidate and bet big on a few verticals | Middling view |
| Challenge | Managing speed and balance | i) Variance in delivery and communication; ii) Bureaucracy; iii) Can Chandra deliver? | Growing customer expectations |

## Page 24 – Managing Brands Longitudinally, Reinforcement, Revitalization, Global Branding, Retail Branding

### Managing Brands Longitudinally

**Reinforcing vs Revitalizing:**

| Reinforcing | Revitalizing |
|---|---|
| Incremental | Evolving |
| Rin det. bar | My father's brand? Yours too! |
| Conservative/Confident | Dynamic |
| Past and present | Present and future |

**Reinforcement–Revitalization–Repositioning–Rebranding is a continuum:**
- Reinforcement – Dettol (protection)
- Revitalization – Bata (your father's shoe to your shoe)
- Repositioning – Marlboro (women to men)
- Rebranding – Accenture (in 147 days)

---

### Managing Brands Longitudinally (Conceptual Overview)

- In which page do you see the whole chapter summarized as an exhibit? See Fig 14-7, 14-8 in p 557, overview of how to read this chapter
- **Longitudinal** – over a period of time (Kantor panel of 80K households)
- **Cross sectional** – at a given point time (m/s of biscuit brands in FY 2024)

**Reinforcing** – brand is good/stuck, re-emphasize old values (Pears)
**Revitalizing** – brand is getting fuddy-duddy, add new values (youth)
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DE6tvZdB3cS8 [1]
- Vicco Vajradanti new look evoked 6 million views
- Old ads focused on ayurveda (product), 'young' not a descriptor for VV

---

### Reinforcing Brands

What products does the brand represent, what need does it satisfy?
Rin added Rose and Lemon, Advanced, bar, liquid & Rinmatic ("wash").
These additions do not fundamentally change the brands.
They add product variants (options) and product forms (price points).
They re-emphasize "food" and "wash".

**How to make the products superior?**
- Mamy Poko pants style diapers
- 15 year warranty for A Duracell battery [18]

---

### Reinforcement – Brand Consistency

Consistency has two aspects:

i) **Consistency of marketing support**
   Managing an FMCG launch – spend crores for 10 yrs, not bother.
   All multinational brands do that (Kellogg's, McDonalds, Dominoes).

ii) **Consistency of associations**
   How much consistency is desirable?
   A brand will and must change incrementally all the time.
   Extended associations change, core associations remain.
   Pears – skin care remains; winter care, weaning soap might change.

Changes are tactical, strategic position remains the same, meaning?
Tactics – 4Ps are tweaked, word owned by the brand doesn't change.

---

### Reinforcement – Brand Consistency (Santoor Example)

What is the conceptual question in the Santoor example?
The brand is an example of "revitalizing" probably.
It is listed in the reinforcement section!
Because all the details of brand history may not be known.

**Brand flashbacks, means what?**
Retro-branding, Retro-advertising, Nostalgia marketing.
Drawing from the associations of the past.

1) Coke Vanilla – https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1BiPVwZe7TU [4] [0:30 onwards]
2) Instax cameras which turn using photo film into retro and nostalgia
   https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=M6afQRzdpu [0:25 to 0:50]
   Ultimate Guide to the Fujifilm Instax Mini 11 w/ SHOOTING TIPS!, 650,898 views, 27 Nov 2020

Stephen Brown's book on "Retromarketing" (post-modern literature).
There is nothing new in marketing?! – Style, Fashion, Fad – p378, K-K.
Style (recurs), Fashion (declines slowly), Fad (drops abruptly).

---

### Reinforcement – Retromarketing

This is true in some cases, e.g.:
i) Style – men's trousers – parallels, narrow cut, bell bottom
   Women's clothes – flowery designs of the 70s coming back
   Vinyl records, Parker ink pens and Yamaha pianos
   Nostalgia can have intergenerational customers
   See 'Devil comes back – Onida'
   New icons like Marvel are there, but older ones like Hanuman do well
   Marvel is futuristic, Hanuman is mythology (past)

**Brand crises sometimes forces such changes:**
i) Galaxy Note 7 recalled all of its phones owing to battery fire
   Aimed at 100% recall, achieved 96% in 3 months [5]
ii) Whatsapp user phone numbers were found on Google searches [6]
iii) PR crisis is a video away; kid's hand stuck in Mall escalator

---

### Reinforcement – Protecting Sources of Equity

**Fortifying vs Leveraging:**
What does this mean?
How far to invest in the brand, how far to harvest it?

- TSMC invested for decades in manufacturing competencies
- Unlike other companies like ARM (no mfg), Intel (both design and mfg)
- TSMC decided to stick to fabrication
- Even today they invest heavily in R&D
- One of the handful of companies to make 5nm chips, now 3 nm chips
- ASML worked with the chip machine making technology for 40 years [20]
- Their latest NA machine costs 350 million $
- It is as big as a bus or flat in Netherlands, it is a Dutch company
- Why is this company so important? The US is leaning on Dutch Govt to prevent tech transfer to Chinese
- 40 years of fortification, i.e. R&D work on slow burn, leveraging e.g.?
- Franchises – McDonald's or KFC, that is milking the brand

---

### Reinforcement – Supporting Marketing Program

**Imagery related associations:**
Symbolic, experiential benefits, user imagery, usage imagery.
Imagery can relate to the real or ideal user.

Some imagery related descriptors of luxury brands:
Indulgence, snobbery, classy, exclusive, status, image, rarity, premium quality, elite, scarce, unique, heritage, craftsmanship, aesthetics, personalized, timeless, desirable, niche, sophisticated, subjective, tasteful, experiential (luxury only vs premium also)

---

### 2.0 – Revitalization

**Two paths to revitalization:**
i) Expanding breadth and depth brand awareness
ii) Improve strength, favorability and uniqueness of brand associations

**2.1 Expanding Awareness**
- Depth of awareness means what? Recognition, recall, how many details and time taken to remember
- **Breadth of occasions** means what? Range of purchase, usage occasions in which it is thought of
  1) Moov (pain specialist)
  2) "Ek beam, teen kaam" – which brand? (headache, cold, joint pain)
  3) Dettol's 6 uses behind the bottle (cuts, shaving, nappies, surgery, etc.)
  4) Colgate Total's 8 benefits listed on the pack
- You can see how brands expand the scope of usage (1 to 8), how far?

---

### Revitalization – Two Ways to Increase Consumption

a) **First is to increase the occasions**, as shown in Moov, Zandu, Dettol

b) **Find new uses for the product** (often by customers):
   1) Baby milk powder used for making sweets in Western India
   2) How LCV became Ace Magic

c) **Increase quantity per occasion** (is this reinforcement?):
   1) Giving discounts
   2) Increasing the pack size per use, by pricing it smartly
      Instead of 8 ml sachet, give 12 ml shampoo
   3) Get 5 for the price of 3 (Amazon style)
   4) Reminder ads that show why more quantity should be consumed
   5) In Covid time wash hands for 20 seconds (normally we do less than that)
   - How many of these are revitalization? They sound like reinforcement!

---

### Managing Target Segment

**Retaining vulnerable customers:**
i) For instance, in telecom and cell phones customers are very fickle.
   Constantly add new, exciting service to keep the service attractive.
ii) Vulnerability might be from lack of ability to pay:
   a) Indus Valley report – bottom 50% contribute to 15% of GDP [21]
   b) 4 wheelers sell, 2 wheelers don't
   c) Villas sell, affordable housing doesn't! (land prices)
   d) Pvt sector not investing, 75% RBI capacity utilization figures
   - Will the income tax concessions make a difference to consumption?
   - The base is too small (only 2.24% or 1.6 crore people pay tax) [22]
   - How to trigger consumption? Agriculture, construction, textiles, assembling, tourism
   - Venice and Dubai together probably get more foreign travelers than India…

---

### Managing Target Segment (cont.)

i) Air India, Wipro, Asian Paints changed logos
ii) Guess what these brands became [17]:

| Old Name | New Name |
|---|---|
| Burbn | Instagram |
| Confinity | Paypal |
| Foodiebay | Zomato |
| Backrub | Google |
| Odeo | Twitter |
| Relentless | Amazon |
| Auctionweb | E-bay |
| Matchbox | Tinder |

---

### Finally…

Typically, brands use both reinforcement as well as revitalization.
While some elements of the brand are played up, others are played down.
Nuances are added.

Over a period of time, suppose a brand incrementally changes…
…and becomes something very different from what it was, then?
So be it, that is what customers want.
It will not be seen as radical because it is ever so slow.

**Limitations of the chapter?**
i) Dividing line between reinforcement and revitalization not clear
ii) Some theory listed under revit. probably goes into reinf.
   Expanding breadth and depth of awareness
iii) Examples need revisiting – Santoor, Old Monk, Royal Enfield

---

### Reinforcement – Summary

**Reinforcing** – brand is good, re-emphasize old values (Pears)
**Revitalizing** – brand is getting fuddy-duddy, add new values

**I) Reinforcement is about a) and b):**
a) What products does the brand represent, what need does it satisfy?
   These additions do not change the brand, they re-emphasize the "old"

b) How to make the products superior?

**II) Reinforcement is about maintaining consistency:**
- Consistency of marketing support: How long can you support the brand without returns?
- Consistency of associations: Core associations remain, extended associations change

**III) Reinforcement is sometimes "retro":**
Retro-branding, Retro-advertising, Retro marketing, Nostalgia marketing.
Style, Fashion, Fad.

**IV) Reinforcement means protecting sources of brand equity:**
To fortify or leverage? How long to invest, when to milk.

**V) Reinforcement marketing program means underscoring one of the two:**
Performance related associations (product focused, internal)

---

### Revitalization – Summary

**Two paths to revitalization:**
I) Expanding breadth and depth brand awareness
II) Improve brand image

**I) Expanding breadth and depth of awareness:**
Improve recognition & recall so that you can…
Increase range of purchase, usage occasions through…
a) Increase occasions of purchase
b) Find new uses for the product
c) Increase quantity per occasion (reinforcement?)

**II) Improving brand image by:**
Improving strength, favorability and uniqueness of brand associations:
1) Retaining vulnerable customers
2) Recapturing lost customers
3) Identifying neglected segments
4) Attracting new customers

---

### What is a Global Brand?

**Define a global brand?**
- Brands whose positioning, advertising strategy, personality, look and feel are in most respects the same from one country to another… are global (Aaker and Joachimstahler, 1999)
- ["Global"] is defined as the multi-market reach of products that are perceived as the same brand worldwide both by consumers and internal constituents (Johansson and Ronkainen, 2005)
- Global brands are those that have global awareness, availability, acceptance, and desirability and are often found under the same name with consistent positioning, image, personality, look, and feel in major markets enabled by standardized and centrally coordinated marketing strategies and programs (Özsomer et al., 2012)

---

### What Changes in a Global Brand

A global brand has similar or same positioning all over the world.
Then how do you accommodate changes every country asks for?

- **Positioning is strategic** – that remains
- For e.g., if Coke's positioning is "happiness" that stays
- But **4Ps are tactical**, they can and do change
- Positioning is strategic, 4Ps are more tactical

**What changes is execution, meaning 4Ps:**
a) For instance, in India the product was probably made stronger
   That appeals to the Indian palette
b) Pricing sometimes tweaked through offerings like "Chota Coke"
c) Indian distribution is more bottle driven & less dispenser driven
d) Finally, having a local communicating in a local idiom
   Aamir Khan variously appeared as a Gorkha, Bihari…

---

### What is a Global Product?

**Challenge in globalizing the product:**
Each country asks for a different product (195 countries).
How will you handle that variety?
Platform approach – Horizontal vs vertical differentiation?

**Globalizing at the product level:**
i) Robust design (sun glass), IT tools (Microsoft OS, Teams)
ii) Aspirational brands (Prada)
iii) Mass manufacturer (all < 10$ products are Chinese, Levitt)
iv) Ethnic local = global (Chinese/Italian food)
v) Cascading the product, sell in reachable markets first
   Beetle from US to Latin America after 18 years
   **Waterfall vs Sprinkler?**

**Globalizing at the assembly level** (mentioned, details cut off)

---

### Globalizing the Product (Table)

| | Local | Global | Standard |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Product variety** | One per country (Many) | Basic Platforms (A few) – *Ohmae* | Same product (one) – *Levitt* |
| **Illustration** | Food | Car theft in Kerala | Abhloy lock |
| | | Whirlpool / *Ford – radiator cap* | Ford T only |

**Mindset:**
| | Local | Global | Standard |
|---|---|---|---|
| Mindset | Polycentric? | Geocentric? | Ethnocen.? |
| Example | Nestle (1.4%) | Cat (46.5%) | Cat (40%) |
| | Stanchart (10%) | | |

**Are some products more globalizable than others? Why?**

| Market | Local | Global/Disposable |
|---|---|---|
| | Glass syringe | Disposable syringe [9] |
| | 2 wheeler lubricant | Ship lubricant |

---

### Global Pricing

i) Global brands are priced at a premium usually.
   But premium not possible in every country, what to do then?
   You can be premium compared to local brands.
   But you may not get the premium you want.
   Almost all multinational brands dropped their price in India.
   Several MNC car brands failed in India due to this reason.

ii) Can you set different prices in different countries?
   **Price corridor**, no country goes beyond the band.

iii) Different products/brands for different countries, e.g.?
   Crest not there in India, but available in the West.

iv) Developing new products ground up, **"Reverse innovation"**
   GE Mac ECG in India at 1000$ (one half of US cost) [7]

---

### Global Communication – When Standardized?

i) When a standard ad works?
   Ad is translation, everything other than language is the same.
   P&G ads in India in early 2000s had S.E. faces!

ii) Simple tag line ("The real thing")

iii) Similar concerns (God, I am getting old!)

iv) Same ad agency (rationalization vs localization)

v) What is this ad an example of?
   - https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Bczjj6nHjkA
   - DHL Ad bird and cat
   - https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Qe7LN3dzS0
   - DHL TV spots bird vs cat
   - **Culture free ads, hence; Ref: Tepstra and Sarathy, p455**

---

### Global Communication – When Customized?

a) **Single biggest factor that forces customization?**
   Language difference – "Nothing sucks like an Electrolux" [8]
   How to ensure this doesn't happen? Retranslate!

b) Govt controls – Pepsi's ad in Middle East
   **3 types of ads:**
   i) Export ads (standardized) – French fmcg bottle in French
      Distinction French cosmetics have that other countries don't?
      They are premium simply because they are French
   ii) Prototype ads (hybrid) – principles laid down, compliance depends on local conditions
   iii) Guideline ads (localized) – only guidelines given, ad developed locally

c) Economic differences (how much opulence to show in ads)

d) Media Availability (internet availability – online ads)

e) Local distributors (favoring a certain kind of communication)

f) **Consumer taste/attitudes (single biggest stumbling block?)**
   i) Volkswagen ad in Italy – this car is different [3]
      Showcased as a black sheep in a herd of normal ones
      In Italy the color stands for independence, so msg goes through
      In other countries black sheep means something else!
   ii) Kit Kat is positioned in UK as ("have a break, have a Kitkat")
      In Norway it is positioned as *Kvikk Lunsj* ("quick lunch")

---

### Global Distribution

i) US (85%) and UK (80%) retailing is organized [5]
   India is splintered like many developing countries (9%)
   How many shops in India stock FMCG goods? **1 crore**

ii) In US Starbucks is a hangout.
   In China, if you don't drink coffee after a while… asked to leave!

iii) Japan's distribution is very peculiar and complicated.
   Small retailers are protected by law.
   Distribution is also many layered, price paid by customers is high.
   Small stores a/c for 59% food sales in Japan (37% in US) [6]

iv) In Africa Nestle distributes by foot, by bike, by taxi [6]

v) In UK, Tesco likely to provide retail banking in its stores

vi) In Brazil, Carrefour reduced its SKUs

vii) Morocco & Italy use specialty stores with narrow product lines.
   In Finland it is the opposite.

viii) Mitsukoshi in Japan attracts 1,00,000 customers a day.
   Ibadan market in Nigeria has 3000 one or 2 person stalls.

ix) In South Africa 1000 stores control 60% of grocery trade.
   The other 40% is spread over 30000 stores, **single stick sales!**

**Conclusions: Distribution is always local, much as you may try to standardize it.**

---

### Global Brand – Conclusion

How to manage a global brand? Want to summarize?

i) **Positioning** is same or similar all over the world
ii) **Globalizing product** – how to platformize?
iii) **Globalizing price** – Managing the price corridor
iv) **Globalizing promotion** – prototype ads, principles laid down
v) **Globalizing place** – localize distribution

---

### Retail Branding – Overview

A slide with two-column format:

**Brand orientation** (strategic) | **Positional advantage** (tactical)
- About the retail brand | About the retail store
- What brand can do for store | What store can do for brand
- Strategy | Tactics
- How can you use the diagram? Du Pont analysis of a retail chain
- Summarize the article in a couple of lines? BO leads to PA, PA leads to performance, true?

---

### Distinctiveness – 3 Broad Types of Retail Experience (Pecoraro & Uusitalo, 2014)

i) **Pragmatic store** (like a library – Metro)
   It is functional, with virtually no help, emotionally neutral
   Uniform graphics, ordinary furniture, watchword – "figure out"

ii) **Romantic store** (like grandmother's house – Fab India)
   It is symbolic, a few friendly staff, emotionally loaded
   Colorful, eco-friendly, traditional furniture, watchword – "celebrate"

iii) **Modern store** (like a health resort – my e.g.: Decathlon)
   It is both functional and symbolic, professional staff
   Minimalist graphics, modern furniture, watchword – "add value"

---

### Distinctiveness – How Does Decathlon Stand Out?

- Enter a dead mall! [N]
- How is D a variant in today's world? [P]
- It basically gets 80% of its revenue offline [Q]
- Their affordable products and disrupted unorganized market
- They compete with Nike, Adidas and Reebok together in India
- Endowment effect – if you touch and feel, you feel like an owner…
- …and become one
- 37% of D's customers are walk by, JLA buyers
- Their employees are sports enthusiasts who do not hard sell
- Products made within the country, no fancy endorsements
- Products technically, at least incrementally better, 50 gm hiking T-shirt
- A camp tent that can be put up in 2 sec, unlike 20 min, 10 yrs back
- How a sweet shop in Bombay is trying to differentiate

---

### Augmentation – IKEA India

**They customized furniture for different cities in India:**
- An average home in Hyderabad is twice the size of that in Bombay
- So, they stock more sofa-cum-beds in Bombay
- Indians prefer closed storage because of dust
- So, Ikea offers glass cabinets and cupboards
- They offered customized cookware like stainless steel idli cookers
- Footfalls have risen to several million a day
- Up to 60 million visitors shopped online in 2021
- While sales have grown, profits are some distance away

Susanne Pulverer spoke to Dilshad Irani, CNBC TV18, 27 Jan 2024.
See the word file "Susan Pulverer's interview……" for details.
50% of Indians say their home is their favorite place to be and 63% of Indians shared that they feel positive about their current life at home.

**(Ikea's 10th life at home report – downloadable 2018 to 23)**
Also available Ikea life at home report imagines life in 2030.
Btw check their India catalogue as well [L].
9 out of 10 Indian think their storage space doesn't look great.

When asked who is your Indian customer, what do you think S said?
Everybody… (we are) very inviting and inclusive… diverse country with many household incomes.
(So) 1000 products already < 200 Rs, working on dropping prices in another 250 by 20%.
If nothing we want them to try food at Ikea!
Where we are currently present …. (customers) a little bit on the younger side ….but…in store you will see all kinds of customers.

**Basically offline (touch and feel), then online.**
Decathlon, Ikea, Caratlane (shop should be good for online to take off).

---

### Symbolism in Retail

**An e.g. of symbolism in global retail?**
Abercrombie and Fitch – what does this retail chain stand for?
**Stands for "young" and "sexy"**
Clearly targets the adolescent crowd in US (see 2012 A&F ad)
How do you operationalize the positioning?
- Shop assets are good looking colleagues
- They wear the garment and model for you
- Catalogues, promo material – pretty raunchy
- A. & F. @ Hawaii – the boy and the girl
- Extreme differentiation backfires, brand in trouble

**An e.g. of symbolism in India retail?**
- "Happily Unmarried" [3] (morphed to "Ustra", wonder why!)

---

### Symbolism – Others

- Word "Happily Unmarried" wants to own – fun
- Word "Chumbak" wants to own – cute

**Tantra T-shirts – caption:**
i) Kid maths – butter + fly = butterfly
ii) Flipkart Monday, Snapdeal Tuesday, Jabong Wednesday, Amazon Thursday, **BANKRUPT, Friday!**

Or

See "Calm more than Kaam"

---

### Retail Branding – Summary

**Three components to retail branding (Fig 1):**
i) Brand orientation
ii) Positional advantage
iii) Organizational performance

The above three components have 9 sub-components.
How do we know the definitions of components and sub-components? Check Table 4.

- **Brand orientation** – what the brand can do for the store? (strategic)
- **Positional advantage** – What the store can do for the brand? (tactical)

**Org. performance = financial performance + strategic effectiveness**
- Financial performance is short term
- Strategic effectiveness is long term
- **Financial performance** = RoI, RoA, Gross Margins, shop level metrics
- **Strategic performance** = Financial objectives + Strategic objectives
- Both objectives are defined from long term point of view

---

### Glossary – Cult Branding (Part 1)

New words encountered in the cult branding article.
We will get them out of the way.
Then I will tell you the big story of cult branding.

i) **Boundaries?**
   Membership of a cult brand is restricted among the followers, e.g.?
   Only those who read all Harry Potter books are called Potterheads

ii) **Ideology**
   A belief strongly held, e.g.?
   A&F is for beautiful people

iii) **Spotlight?**
   It conducts dramatic events to hold your attention, e.g.?
   Woodstock for Rock, Madras Music Academy for Carnatic Class[ical music]

iv) **Lovebombing?**
   Once you are inside the fold its followers shower love on you, e.g.?
   H.O.G. and how they help each other

v) **Pyramid?**
   Among the followers all are equal, but some are more equal, e.g.?
   Sudhir Choudhary gives 1000 litchis to Sachin every year
   Sachin sponsors his tickets for every match of his

vi) **In-the-know MARCOMM?**
   Communication is scarce, deliberate and carefully targeted, e.g.?
   Warren Buffet writes annually one letter to his shareholders
   It is eagerly awaited and goes viral almost as soon as it is aired
   What is the price of one share of Berkshire Hathway?
   **$702,250.00 – just one share!** (NYSE, after close, Nov 13, 5:05:01)

vii) **Turn tables?**
   If something goes wrong, it is always the customer's mistake…
   Not the brand's!, e.g.?
   Starbucks suddenly closes down, says…
   "We are training to make perfect coffee, wait…."
   And customers wait
   Bullet gets you to wait for the next vehicle and you do

viii) **Big Brother?**
   There is always some enemy waiting to malign the cult, or so it is said, e.g.?
   How dare you blame Narendra Modi?
   Demonetization? GST botch, 6 year stagnant exports
   Maybe he forgot us…(migrants who walked back)

---

### 5 Stages of a Cult Brand

i) Brand consideration
ii) Brand affiliation
iii) Brand admiration
iv) Brand adoration
v) Brand obsession

"What I am showing you is what I learnt after reading 115 articles"

---

### 1. Brand Consideration

**What in your view is step 1 for a cult brand?**
- The brand has "extreme differentiation" (Modi, Buddha, IIT)
- The brand displays a very different DNA
- 2 distinct markers of cult brand in "brand consideration"
- **Without these 2, the brand can never grow into a cult brand… no matter what it does later**

i) Extreme differentiation
ii) Unafraid of taking risks
   - Beatles performed in Shea stadium…
   - …though it was unsuitable for music, it was a sell out!
iii) Sells a lifestyle and not a product
   - Who is Barbara Millicent Williams? Barbie – not just a doll
   - It is who you want to be, when you grow up

---

### 2. Brand Affiliation

**ii) Formation of brand community**
Brand Community is "a specialized, non-geographically bound community" (Muniz and O'Guinn, 2001).
It has "influentials" (donors of opinion) who communicate and "susceptibles" (receivers of opinion) (Aral & Walker, 2012).
This leads to word-of-mouth communication.

**iii) Brand communication**
A brand should communicate its ideology and identity.
In the initial stages the company takes lead in forming groups.
"My Starbucks Idea" networks with customers to source ideas from them for the brand.
H.O.G. has a million Harley Davidson members.

---

### 3. Brand Admiration

**2 constituents of brand admiration:**
i) Generation of positive word-of-mouth (wom)
ii) Followers become fans

**i) What triggers positive wom, getting the message viral?**
The message needs to be:
a) Useful/perceived to be useful (heart attack!)
b) Teaser (are you in a hurry, see this list of 35 things?)
c) Fun (Ice bucket challenge, Kolavari)

---

### 4. Brand Adoration

Brand adoration stage is marked by the following:
a) Customers spend time, money, energy for the brand (attachment)
b) They openly flaunt consumption of the brand

**i) Brand community becomes sub-culture**
A sub-culture is a set of people strongly focused on a matter of common interest, in this case the brand (Schouten & McAlexander, 1993).

**ii) Brand language. E.g.?**
Group members develop a private language of their own.
i) IIMC students call themselves "Jokars"

---

### 5. Brand Obsession?

**I) Obsession is a passionate pursuit that doesn't care about results.**
It is characterized by:
i) An unconditional pursuit
ii) Uncharacteristic passion
iii) Consumption as a quasi-religious experience

**II) This obsession manifests itself as memorabilia, e.g.?**
i) Building shrines (221 B Baker's Street)
ii) Going on pilgrimages (Oscar ramp walk)
iii) Designing tightly defined rituals (licking cream of Oreo biscuits)
iv) Celebrating brand myths (Marlboro and number of cowboys)
v) Making consumption a sacred act (HD Manual – Forbes 2001 art.)
vi) Fans erected a 30ft-tall cut-out of Lionel Messi in a river in K'kode
vii) Strange, but true. A bunch of people married their Mazda Miatas [1]

---

### Cult Brand vs Good Brand (Full Comparison)

**Are cult brands a more advanced form of a good brand? Or are they basically different?**

| **Good Brand** | **Cult Brand** |
|---|---|
| Offers more functional benefits | Offers more self-expressive and emotional benefits |
| First stage | Final stage |
| Loyalty, Trust | Obsession |
| Word of mouth | Evangelism, Fanaticism |
| Customer | Convert |
| Good Connect | Separation anxiety |
| Happy, satisfied | Proud, Uplified, Transcendent |
| Fans | Fanatics |
| Secular rituals | Sacred rituals |
| Community | Sub culture, Tribalism |
| Delightful experience | Transformative experience |
| Customers love it | Customers own it |
| Customers of brand | Trustees/guardians of the brand |
| Strong engagement with brand | Deep engagement with brand |
| Typical e.g.: Amazon | Typical e.g.: Harley Davidson |

**Good brand =**
Differentiated offering + Distinct positioning + Loyalty

**Cult brand =**
Maverick offering + Provocative positioning + Obsession

---

### Cult Brand vs Good Brand (Final)

**Cult brand =**
Reputed/well-known/good brand + Faith/Obsession/Devotion/Fanaticism

Sacralization of a good brand is a must for it to become a cult brand.

**In sum:**
> A cult brand is a secular substitute for a religious symbol.

---

*End of Slides — All 24 pages converted.*

## SESSION: PRINCIPLES OF BRAND EXTENSION

### Types of Brand Extension [Page 1]

**PRINCIPLES OF BRAND EXTENSION**

**TYPES OF BRAND EXTENSION**
Under how many headings can all the brand extensions in the world be classified?

**Diagram: Classification of Brand Extensions**
A branching diagram with two categories from marketing literature (Mark. lit.) mapped to a classification system with illustrations:

| Mark. lit. | Our Classification | Illustration |
|---|---|---|
| Line Extension | Product Related | Gillette Mach3, Vector |
| Brand Extension | Image Related | Gillette skincare soln. |
| Brand Extension | Unrelated | Gillette telecom! |

- Line Extension maps to Product Related
- Brand Extension branches into two: Image Related and Unrelated

---

### Brand Extendability [Page 2]

**Brand Extendability**

**Formula brand** — Dhara, Lifebuoy, Colgate

Adjective common to water purifier and vacuum cleaner?
*Clean*
Adjective common to lighter, ball pen and razor?
*Disposable*
What are the brand names?

**Know-how brand** — Eureka Forbes, Bic
Amul (food), Asian Paints (décor)

**Interest brand** — Disney (entertainment)
Google (digital)

**Philosophy brand** — Tata, Samsung, Amazon (future?)

---

### Summary – Brand Extensions (Part 1) [Pages 3–4]

**Summary**

5 implications of extensions
Good, more good, bad, ugly, more ugly

Pros of brand extensions
Known name, easy recognition, favourable associations rub off

Cons of brand extensions
Parent comes with a baggage, it is not cheaper

What product category to stretch into?
Based on 6 criteria
i) Market attractiveness ii) brand value consistency
iii) Orgn.al strengths iv) Internal-external fit v) customers
vi) Managing 4Ps
Check brand value consistency (item ii) with customers
Is hair oil close to shampoo?

*(Note: Pages 3 and 4 show the same slide content, page 4 being a clearer version. Page 4 adds the note: "is hair oil close to shampoo?" is NOT present on the clearer version, suggesting it may have been cut off.)*

---

### Summary – Brand Extensions (Part 2) [Page 5]

**Summary**

In India, adverse impact of extension failure on parent doesn't seem to be high

Three classifications of extensions
Line (same product) vs Brand (different product)
Product rel (Cinthol soap), Image rel (talc), Unrelated (TV)
Vertical (different prices) vs Horizontal (different products)

Formula brands difficult to stretch, philosophy brands easy

Paradox of brand extensions
If the parent is too strong or too weak it cannot be stretched

Product related extensions
i) How many variants in product related extensions?
How many do you think will customers remember?

---

### Summary – Brand Extensions (Part 3) [Pages 6–7]

**Summary**

ii) What to do about cannibalization?
Design for 20% cannibalization

iii) Upward or downward extension?
What is the "word" the parent owns is key

Unrelated extensions
i) Unrelated extensions are possible in philosophy brands
Question is, how many extensions (GE? Gucci?)

*(Page 7 – clearer version adds:)*
Bigger question, will they make money?
ii) Unrelated extensions sit best on orgn.al or family names

## SESSION: BRAND ARCHITECTURE / BRAND RELATIONSHIP SPECTRUM

### House of Brands – Not Connected and Shadow Endorser [Pages 8–9]

**Not connected**
Parent doesn't want customer to know
Prefer you not to know the connect

**Shadow endorser**
Parent doesn't tell you, but you get to know
Company doesn't mind if u know the connect

---

### House of Brands – Unconnected (Examples) [Page 9]

House of brands is in 2 types – i) unconnected ii) shadow endorser

**House of Brands – Unconnected**
i) Natraj and Apsara unconnected to Hind Pencils
ii) Reckitt Benckiser's brands Dettol, Moov and Cherry Blossom do not mention it in ads
iii) Volkswagen India doesn't mention Audi

Give an example from India?

What is the plus of this strategy?
It is less risky – conservative branding

---

### Shadow Endorser (Examples) [Pages 10–11]

**Shadow endorser** — House of brands

JLR and Tata, Yardley and Wipro
- https://wiproconsumercare.com/brands-india/
- https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6iBYorifYno

### Brand Portfolio Structure [Page 18]

**Brand portfolio structure**

**Brand groupings means?**
How can the brands be grouped together
How many segments are my brands covering?

**Why should we examine brand groupings?**
Will tell you what opportunities you are covering across products
By prices (Harrier – hp, Tiago – affordable)
By product (cars, multi-utility vehicles, cross-overs)
By quality (designer/premium)
By design (classic – Safari, contemporary – Altroz)

**Brand groupings**
Vini cosmetics (Darshan Patel – read about him, Krack, Moov)
Vini divides its portfolio into 3 types of products
i) Look good (powders – White Tone face powder)
ii) Do good (anti-ageing for 40+ – Prepair4050)
iii) Smell good (deos – Fogg)

|---|---|---|---|

### Summary – Brand Relationship Spectrum [Page 20]

**Summary**

**Brand relationship spectrum**
9 types of relationships between the parent and the brand
From house of brands to branded house

i) House of brands (unconnected)
Parent doesn't want the customer to know the connect
Reckitt and its brands Cherry Blossom, Moov, Dettol

ii) House of brands (shadow endorser)
Parent doesn't tell customer, customer gets to know, that is OK
Implicit endorsement
Titan and Sonata (Titan not mentioned, OK if the customer knows)

iii) Token endorser
[Text partially cut off at bottom]
Explicit endorsement, though faint
...appears discreetly at the end of the ad

---

### Summary – Brand Relationship Spectrum (cont.) [Pages 21–22]

*(Page 21 – partially obscured by screen sharing toolbar at top)*

iv) Lin[ked name] [partially obscured]
Compound name of parent and brand
McAloo Tikki

v) Strong endorser
Parent seen in conjunction with brand, though at some distance
Ethnix by Raymond

vi), vii) Sub brands
Parent and brand seen next to each other
Co-driver – Parent = brand (Godrej No 1)
Master brand as driver – Parent > brand (Music systems)
Brand as driver – Brand > Parent (Indica?)

viii), ix) Branded house
Parent = brand name
Same identity – all products have same value proposition (LG)
Different identity – diff products have diff value propositions (Tata)

### Summary – Brand Architecture (4 Elements) [Pages 22–23]

**Summary –** 4 elements

i) Brand rel. with parent – Product market context roles (spectrum)
ii) Brand rel. with siblings – Brand portfolio structure
iii) Brand rel. with itself – Portfolio graphics
iv) Brand portfolio roles – is this architecture profitable?
Brand relationship spectrum is a subset of brand architecture
i) and iii) already covered

**Brand portfolio structure**
Brand relationship with siblings – 3 components

a) Brand range (similar to product scope)
How far the brand can extend without encroaching on siblings?
Nexon? Tata Nexon? New brand name?

b) Brand hierarchy trees
Family tree of the parent, brand and siblings (Tata or Colgate tree)

c) Brand groups
How many opportunities did the brand and siblings exhaust?
Vini cosmetics – Look good, Do good, Smell good
Pepsi – Fun for you, Good for you, Better for you

**Brand portfolio roles**
Is the architecture profitable?
Silver bullet – brings fame – Java for Sun
Linchpin – sales tomorrow, profit tomorrow – Benz self driving trucks
Strategic – sales today, profit tomorrow – EV brands for car co.s
Cash cow – sales today, profit today – Lorries for Tatas

### Product Brand vs Corporate Brand [Page 25]

**Product Brand vs Corporate Brand**

**Diagram description:** A comparison table with 8 rows:

| Subject | Product Brand | Corporate Brand |
|---|---|---|
| Nature | Tangible: Can be Experienced? | Intangible |
| Focus attention on | The product | The company |
| Driven by | Middle Management? | Top Management |
| Target Audience | Customers | Multiple stakeholders |
| Delivered by | Marketing / Sales Dept | Whole company |
| Communication Mix | Marketing communication | Integrated corporate communication (Internal / External) |
| Time Horizon | Short (Life of the product)? | Long (Life of the company) |
| Importance to company | Functional? | Strategic |

### Corporate Philosophy [Pages 26–27]

**Inputs**
**Corporate philosophy:**
Corporate brand is an expression of corporate strategic intent (Urde, 1999)
Gillette wanted to be technology leader
Good corporate philosophy grabs the soul of its employees (Collins & Porras, 1991)
Corporate philosophy is different from goals which are tactical and SMART (?)
Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Relevant and Timebound

**The Tata perspective**
More Indians are suffering from lack of opportunities than lack of food – JRD

*(Page 27 – clearer/expanded version adds:)*
Indians are capable of delivering great results given an opportunity
In Sweden airport staff used to set their watches to Indian Airlines flight landing
J R D himself used to check the brightness of spoons, how hostesses smiled
How Mulgaonkar built the first truck
Fredrick Upcott – What? Indians making steel? (Creation of Wealth – R. M Lala)
What are core values?

### Corporate Culture [Page 30]

**Corporate culture?**
Corp culture for an agile organization follows 3 laws (Dunning, 2018)
i) law of the small team ii) law of the customer iii) law of the network

You are an outsider, how do you infer culture of a co.?

**i) Go by what they do, not what they say?**
a) Narayana Murthy – paying for wife, process for resolution, beautifying building, one of the directors fined, Gold standard of guidance, on NASDAQ not for money
b) Multinationals – did they buy property in India or lease?
"Against all odds, the IT story of India" – Kris Gopalakrishnan et. al., 2022

**ii) Is there a tangible indicator that can signal e.g. integrity?**
How clean are their accounts?
40% of Indian companies' accounts are suspect (Saurabh Mukherjea)
How do you check them?
Forensic accounting, get some CAs, CFAs trained in this [text cut off]

---

### Product Communication – Tata Group Case Study [Page 31]

**Product communication – what do you think of their product comm.?**
Given the diffuse nature of the Tata group
A centralized corporate biased communication was inevitable
Traditionally corporate identity was diffuse across Tata group companies
Naturally because the nature of the products, positioning, history
- Tata Taj – subdued, hard selling doesn't work in premium products/services
- Tata tea – aggressive, because the domain is very competitive

Under Ratan Tata the rainbow of products was pushed into corp dominant arch.
Basically, to signal individual company CEOs that the boss is Bombay House!
Move from product and corp dominant arch is in fact HQ trying to assert itself

Conclusions
i) Products and services need domain specific communication (high or low decibel)
ii) A corporate needs to have a semblance of centralization in messaging
iii) What appears as product vs corporate communication might be org.al politics

---

### Employees View – Tata Group [Page 32]

**Employees view – how do you think they rate the group?**
Employees engage at 4 levels (intellectual, social, affective and organizational)
Affective engagement means employees getting energized because of work content
Unless employees trust the corporate brand, customers won't (Yaniv and Farkas, 2005)

How is the engagement in Tatas? – different at different levels
It appears social and organizational engagement is higher than intellectual & affective

**Top rung – which side are you on?**
JRD time vs Ratan's time
**Satraps vs tamed lions**
Darbari Seth, Kerkar (hotels), T'walla (Voltas), R. Modi (Tata steel), P'vala (ACC)
Especially the last two
They ran their companies like their empires under benign gaze of JRD Tata
But Ratan Tata wanted to tame all satraps, become the boss and he did!
Therefore, at different levels employees have different v[iews of the] Tata empire [text cut off]

---

### Products/Services – Tata Group [Pages 33–34]

**Products/Services – how do you think Tata group rates on this?**
What is common to products/services they will enter in future?
a) Technology barrier – exited soaps (TOMCO – Hamam)
b) Investment barrier – Not many Co.s can invest billions in takeovers (Corus)

Wide variety – Steel, auto, IT, salt, drilling, engineering, finance etc
A behemoth with several product and service capabilities
How are they faring in different product categories?
In leading products and services – middling, sometimes struggling

---

*(Page 34)*

R. Jagannathan, Swarajya – when C. Mistry was booted, only 2 Tata co.s were in profits
Tata – a great brand in search of good enough products?, God with clay feet?

Now
All products and services are turning around
Debt reducing across all companies – Tata steel, Tata Motors, Tata Power
Combined market value of Tata's listed affiliates shot up from $140bn (2017) to $400bn in 2024
The group's net debt to income ratio fell from eight in 2020 to just 2.4 [27]
Cars getting more desirable
New superapp Neu (for Tata group shopping and payments)

What are the 6 big, new initiatives of Tata group?
i) Personal care – Studio West (part of Westside), Skinn (part of Titan)
ii) A payment app that competes with Gpay, Phonepe (for all payments)
iii) Qmin – Indian Hotels' home food delivery, food trucks for on-the-go meals
iv) Semi conductor chip manufacturing application to GoI
v) Healthcare – 1 mg, online doctor consultation, medical devices
vi) Edtech – Online education for Class I to X [22]
Btw don't forget the 470 aircraft (!) ordered by Air India

---

### Consumers – Tata Group [Page 35]

**Consumers – how do you think they rate the Tata group?**
Consumers rate different products differently
Presence in multiple categories gives confidence (recollect brand extension)
Yet, literature on umbrella brands says that quality variations……
….across product categories leads to loss of confidence in the parent brand
High variance in delivery inevitable given the range of products/services
That is how conglomerates concede share to competitors
Tata steel yard and Tata mobile connection

**Financial community? (Corp conduct vs stock price)**
Weak correlation globally between corp good behaviour and stock price (Brammer, et al. 2009), (Gok & Ozkaya, 2011)
Similar results are seen in India
Financial analysts respect the Tata group, but they want performance
Each Tata company's is rated purely based on its own results, not the group's
Sometime back when Tata Motors domestic business was not doing well…
…all that analysts were worried about was JLR sales (>400000) [text cut off]

---

### Minority Shareholders and Suppliers – Tata Group [Page 36]

**How do they treat minority shareholders?**
The TVS and Murugappa group have settled family disputes in such a way….
…that the listed companies are not impacted
Therefore, minority shareholders are not impacted by family disputes [24]
Contrast this with Subhas Chandra of Zee TV and his group
Brilliant entrepreneur and a……….. [25]

**Suppliers – how do you think they rate the group?**
Corporate (OEM) reputation matters for suppliers, if…. (Flax et al., 2016).
i) The OEM is ethical and candid in its relationships
ii) The supplier is strategically integrated with OEM

The Indian story is a partial confirmation
No supplier is ever happy in India with a big group to which he supplies
He is at their mercy
Tatas have centralized buying – can you bargain with them for tyre price?
It means one lakh tyres less if they take business elsewhere – do you afford it?

---

### Influential Groups – Tata Group [Page 37]

**Influential groups – how do you think they rate the group?**
Civil society intuitively suspects corporate groups
Corporate groups often use CSR to (Hamann & Acutt, 2003)
i) accommodate (make cosmetic changes to look socially acceptable)
ii) legitimisation (influence public discourse to make corp actions acceptable)
Civil society should engage in 'critical cooperation' not obstructionism

Criticism – Arundhati Roy (Capitalism – a ghost story) vs Aakar Patel

AR – "We all watch Tata Sky, we surf the net with Tata Photon, we ride in Tata taxis, we stay in Tata Hotels, we sip our Tata tea in Tata bone china and stir it with teaspoons made of Tata Steel. We buy Tata books in Tata bookshops. *Hum Tata ka namak khate hain*. We're under siege".

---

### Media – Tata Group [Page 38]

**Media – the asce[ndancy of digital/media]** [partially obscured]
When adverse media coverage hits a firm it should hit back digitally (Fan et.al., 2013)
Toyota's social media coverage, twice as effective as adverse media coverage…
…when it had to recall millions of cars

**Tata group and the media?**
By and large good, despite Nira Radia
Contrast this with Reliance
Most Indian media is scared of Mukesh Ambani, why?
He owns it (e.g. CNN-IBN)
The Economist is not afraid – "The unloved billionaire", 2 Aug 2014
Mukesh Ambani – "Reliance Industries .. role model for Indians who dare to dream"
Economist – "This secretive and politically powerful private empire is not a national champion but an embarrassment"
Tatas by contrast are viewed favorably, by and large
Tatas are respected, Ambanis are feared

## SESSION: MANAGING BRANDS LONGITUDINALLY

### Reinforcing vs Revitalizing [Pages 40–41]

**Managing brands longitudinally**

| Reinforcing | Revitalizing |
|---|---|
| Incremental | Evolving |
| Rin det. bar | My father's brand? yours too! |
| Conservative/Confident | Dynamic |
| Past and present | Present and future |

*(Page 41 – clearer version adds:)*
Reinforcement–Revitalization–Repositioning–Rebranding is a continuum
Reinforcement – Dettol (protection)
Revitalization – Bata (your father's shoe to your shoe)
Repositioning – Marlboro (women to men)
Rebranding – Accenture (in 147 days)

---

### Managing Brands Longitudinally – Introduction [Page 42]

**Managing brands longitudinally**

In which page do you see the whole chapter summarized as an exhibit?
See Fig 14-7, 14-8 in p 557, overview of how to read this chapter

Managing brands longitudinally means?
Longitudinal – over a period of time (Kantor panel of 80K households)
Cross sectional – at a given point time (m/s of biscuit brands in FY 2024)

Reinforcing – brand is good/stuck, re-emphasize old values (Pears)
Revitalizing – brand is getting fuddy-duddy, add new values (youth)
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DE6tvZdBcS8 [1]
Vicco Vajradanti new look evoked 6 million views
Old ads focused on ayurveda (product), 'young' not a descriptor for VV

---

### Reinforcing Brands [Page 43]

**Reinforcing brands**

What products does the brand represent, what need does it satisfy?
Rin added Rose and Lemon, Advanced, bar, liquid & Rinmatic ("wash")
These additions do not fundamentally change the brands
They add product variants (options) and product forms (price points)
They re-emphasize "food' and "wash"

How to make the products superior?
Mamy Poko pants style diapers
15 year warranty for A Duracell battery [18]

---

### Reinforcement – Brand Consistency [Pages 44–45]

**Reinforcement – brand consistency**

Consistency has two aspects
i) Consistency of marketing support
Managing an FMCG launch – spend crores for 10 yrs, not bother
All multinational brands do that (Kellogg's, McDonalds, Dominoes)

ii) Consistency of associations
How much consistency is desirable?
A brand will and must change incrementally all the time
Extended associations changes, core associations remain
Pears – skin care remains; winter care, weaning soap might change

Changes are tactical, strategic position remains the same, meaning?
Tactics – 4Ps are tweaked, word owned by the brand doesn't change

---

*(Page 45)*

**Reinforcement – brand consistency**

What is the conceptual question in the Santoor example?
The brand is an example of "revitalizing" probably
It is listed in the reinforcement section!
Bcos all the details of brand history may not be known

Brand flashbacks, means what?
Retro-branding, Retro-advertising, Nostalgia marketing
Drawing from the associations of the past
1) Coke Vanilla – https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iBiPVwZe7TU [4] [0:30 onwards]
2) Instax cameras which turn using photo film into retro and nostalgia
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=M6afQRzdpII [0:25 to 0:50]
Ultimate Guide to the Fujifilm Instax Mini 11 w/ SHOOTING TIPS!, 650,898 views, 27 Nov 2020

Stephen Brown's book on "Retromarketing" (post-modern literature)
There is nothing new in marketing?! – Style, Fashion, Fad – p378, K-K
Style (recurs), Fashion (declines slowly), Fad (drops abruptly [text cut off])

---

### Reinforcement – Retromarketing [Page 46]

**Reinforcement – retromarketing**

This is true in some cases, e.g.?
i) Style – men's trousers – parallels, narrow cut, bell bottom
Women's clothes – flowery designs of the 70s coming back
Vinyl records, Parker ink pens and Yamaha pianos
Nostalgia can have intergenerational customers
See 'Devil comes back – Onida'
New icons like Marvel are there, but older ones like Hanuman do well
Marvel is futuristic, Hanuman is mythology (past)

Brand crises sometimes forces such changes
i) Galaxy Note 7 recalled all of its phones owing to battery fire
Aimed at 100% recall, achieved 96% in 3 months [5]
ii) Whatsapp user phone numbers were found on Google searches [6]
iii) PR crisis is a video away; kid's hand stuck in Mall escalator

---

### Reinforcement – Protecting Sources of Equity [Page 47]

**Reinforcement – protecting sources of equity**

**Fortifying vs leveraging**
What does this mean?
How far to invest in the brand, how far to harvest it?
TSMC invested for decades in manufacturing competencies
Unlike other companies like ARM (no mfg), Intel (both design and mfg)
TSMC decided to stick to fabrication
Even today they invest heavily in R&D
One of the handful of companies to make 5nm chips, now 3 nm chips

ASML worked with the chip m/c making technology for 40 years [20]
Their latest NA machine costs, 350 million $
It is as big as a bus or flat in Netherlands, it is a Dutch company
Why is this company so important?
The US is leaning on Dutch Govt to prevent tech transfer to Chinese
40 years of fortification, i.e. R&D work on slow burn, leveraging e.g.?
Franchises – McDonald's or KFC, that is milking the brand

---

### Reinforcement – Supporting Marketing Program [Page 48]

**Reinforcement – supporting marketing program**

**Imagery related associations**
Symbolic, experiential benefits, user imagery, usage imagery
Imagery can relate to the real or ideal user

Some imagery related descriptors of luxury brands
Indulgence, snobbery, classy, exclusive, status, image, rarity, premium, quality, elite, scarce, unique, heritage, craftsmanship, aesthetics, personalized, timeless, desirable, niche, sophisticated, subjective, tasteful, experiential (luxury only vs premium also)

---

### 2.0 Revitalization [Page 49]

**2.0 Revitalization**

Two paths to revitalization
i) Expanding breadth and depth brand awareness
ii) Improve strength, favorability and uniqueness of brand associations

**2.1 Expanding awareness**
Depth of awareness means what?
Recognition, recall, how many details and time taken to remember
Breadth of occasions means what?
Range of purchase, usage occasions in which it is thought of
1) Moov (pain specialist)
2) "Ek baarn, teen kaam", which brand? (headache, cold, joint pain)
3) Dettol's 6 uses behind the bottle (cuts, shaving, nappies, surgery etc)
4) Colgate Total's 8 benefits listed on the pack
You can see how brands expand the scope of usage (1 to 8), how far?

---

### Revitalization – Two Ways to Increase Consumption [Page 50]

**Revitalization**

Two ways to increase consumption
a) First is to increase the occasions, as shown in Moov, Zandu, Dettol

b) Find new uses for the product (often by customers)
1) Baby milk powder used for making sweets in Western India
2) How LCV became Ace Magic

c) Increase quantity per occasion (is this reinforcement?)
1) Giving discounts
2) Increasing the pack size per use, by pricing it smartly
Instead of 8 ml sachet, give 12 ml shampoo
3) Get 5 for the price of 3 (Amazon style)
4) Reminder ads that show why more quantity should be consumed
In Covid time wash hands for 20 seconds (normally we do less than that)
How many of these are revitalization? They sound like reinforcement!

---

### Managing Target Segment [Page 51]

**Managing target segment**

**Retaining vulnerable customers**
i) For instance, in telecom and cell phones customers are very fickle
Constantly add new, exciting service to keep the service attractive

ii) Vulnerability might be from lack of ability to pay
a) Indus Valley report – bottom 50% contribute to 15% of GDP [21]
b) 4 wheelers sell, 2 wheelers don't
c) Villas sell, affordable housing doesn't! (land prices)
d) Pvt sector not investing, 75% RBI capacity utilization figures
Will the income tax concessions make a difference to consumption?
The base is too small (only 2.24% or 1.6 crore people pay tax) [22]
How to trigger consumption?
Agriculture, construction, textiles, assembling, tourism
Venice and Dubai together probably get more foreign travelers than India [text cut off]

---

### Managing Target Segment – Rebranding Examples [Page 52]

**Managing target segment**

i) Air India, Wipro, Asian Paints changed logos

ii) Guess what these brands became [17]

| Original Name | Became |
|---|---|
| Burbn | Instagram |
| Confinity | Paypal |
| Foodiebay | Zomato |
| Backrub | Google |
| Odeo | Twitter |
| Relentless | Amazon |
| Auctionweb | E-bay |
| Matchbox | Tinder |

---

### Finally – Reinforcement and Revitalization [Page 53]

**Finally….**

Typically, brands use both reinforcement as well as revitalization
While some elements of the brand are played up, others are played down
Nuances are added

Over a period of time, suppose a brand incrementally changes…
….and becomes something very different from what it was, then?
So be it, that is what customers want
It will not be seen as radical because it is over so slow

Limitations of the chapter?
i) Dividing line between reinforcement and revitalization not clear
ii) Some theory listed under revit, probably goes into reinf.
Expanding breadth and depth of awareness
iii) Examples need revisiting – Santoor, Old Monk, Royal Enfield

---

### Reinforcement – Summary (Part 1) [Page 54]

**Reinforcement – summary**

Reinforcing – brand is good, re-emphasize old values (Pears)
Revitalizing – brand is getting fuddy-duddy, add new values

I) Reinforcement is about a) and b)
a) What products does the brand represent, what need does it satisfy?
These additions do not change the brand, they re-emphasize the "old"
b) How to make the products superior?

II) Reinforcement is about maintaining consistency
Consistency of marketing support
How long can you support the brand without returns?
Consistency of associations
Core associations remain, extended associations change

---

### Reinforcement – Summary (Part 2) [Page 55]

**Reinforcement – summary**

III) Reinforcement is sometimes "retro"
Retro-branding, Retro-advertising, Retro marketing, Nostalgia marketing
Style, Fashion, Fad

IV) Reinforcement means protecting sources of brand equity
To fortify or leverage?
How long to invest, when to milk

V) Reinforcement mkt.ing program means, underscoring one of the two
Performance related associations (product focused, internal)

---

### Revitalization – Summary [Pages 56–57]

**Revitalization – summary**

Two paths to revitalization
I) Expanding breadth and depth brand awareness
II) Improve brand image

I) Expanding breadth and depth of awareness
Improve recognition & recall so that you can….
Increase range of purchase, usage occasions thro'….
a) Increase occasions of purchase
b) Find new uses for the product
c) Increase quantity per occasion (reinforcement?)

II) Improving brand image by
Improving strength, favorability and uniqueness of brand associations
1) Retaining vulnerable customers
2) Recapturing lost customers
3) Identifying neglected segments
4) Attracting new customers

*(Pages 56 and 57 show the same summary slide — page 56 is blurry, page 57 is clearer.)*

---

## SESSION: GLOBAL BRANDING

### What is a Global Brand? [Page 58]

**What is a global brand?**

Define a global brand?
Brands whose positioning, advertising strategy, personality, look and feel are in most respects the same from one country to another …are global (Aaker and Joachimstahler, 1999)

["Global"] is defined as the multi-market reach of products that are perceived as the same brand worldwide both by consumers and internal constituents (Johansson and Ronkainen, 2005)

Global brands are those that have global awareness, availability, acceptance, and desirability and are often found under the same name with consistent positioning, image, personality, look, and feel in major markets enabled by standardized and centrally coordinated marketing strategies and programs (Ozsomer et al., 2012)

---

### What Changes in a Global Brand [Page 59]

**What changes in a global brand**

A global brand has similar or same positioning all over the world
Then how do you accommodate changes every country asks for?

Positioning is strategic that remains
For e.g., if Coke's positioning is "happiness" that stays
But 4Ps are tactical, they can and do change
Positioning is strategic, 4Ps are more tactical

What changes is execution, meaning 4Ps
a) For instance, in India the product was probably made stronger
That appeals to the Indian palette
b) Pricing sometimes tweaked through offerings like "Chota Coke"
c) Indian distribution is more bottle driven & less dispenser driven
d) Finally, having a local communicating in a local idiom
Aamir Khan variously appeared as a Gorkha, Bihari…

---

### What is a Global Product? [Pages 60–61]

**What is a global product?**

Challenge in globalizing the product
Each country asks for a different product (195 countries)
How will you handle that variety?
Platform approach – Horizontal vs vertical differentiation?

**Globalizing at the product level**
i) Robust design (sun glass), IT tools (Microsoft OS, Teams)
ii) Aspirational brands (Prada)
iii) Mass manufacturer (all < 10$ products are Chinese, Levitt)
iv) Ethnic local = global (Chinese/Italian food)
v) Cascading the product, sell in reachable markets first
Beetle from US to Latin America after 18 years
Waterfall vs Sprinkler?

*(Page 61 adds:)*
**Globalizing at the assembly level** [text cut off at bottom]

---

**Globalizing the product**
