# B2B Brands: An Indicative List

**Title:** B2B Brands — An Indicative List
**Author(s):** Prof Y L R Moorthi (implied; internal course material)
**Publication:** Course material for Brand Management
**Year:** Not dated (references events up to approximately 2022)
**Original Filename:** b2b brands - an indicative list.pdf

---

[Page 1]

## B2b brands

Here are some b2b brands worth studying. Remember in b2b brands, the corporate brand and the product brand are often the same. Same is true of many IT and service brands. Other than in consumer products, in all the other categories the product brand is not the prime focus. The corporate brand is. Therefore, studying the companies is inevitable to understand the brand.

> **Note (in red in original):** Besides, the scope of our final exam includes all brands, b2c, b2b, services and IT. You can also be asked to cite a b2b/service/IT example specifically in the question. Which is why I am sending this list. You can use the names given below. But you cannot repeat the details given here. This is just a primer for you. This opens the door to a world we do not normally explore (for some reason branding in the minds of students means just FMCG branding). Read on.

**Gravitas** – is in recycling business of non-ferrous metals (got ESG funding)

**Bharat Dynamics** – the only missile making company in the country

**NALCO's** strengths – i) lowest cost producer in the world ii) never made an EBITA loss even in downturns [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7sZdJbrKS2k; Why To Invest In NALCO Amid High Aluminium Prices | Ideas For Profit, 87 views, 2 Mar 2022]

Check this video to now about these unusual companies – **MTAR and Policure**
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y4Ro8gCDAwE
Delve In To The Business Strategies Of MTAR Technologies | Inside Out | CNBC TV18, 4,364 views, 3 Jan 2022

> **Note (in red/magenta in original):** Ordnance Factory Board (Govt of India undertaking that makes everything from infantry to boots for army jawans) will now be broken into 7 companies (see http://ofb.gov.in/ for the list). This will fundamentally change the defence sector procurement in India. It is going to get extremely competitive. Good for the country! Follow these 7 companies and their respective competitors. You will know all the Indian companies in this space (L&T, Mahindras, Tata Technologies, Bharat Forge and so on).
> Check out this video to know why and how: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KWB-guTM3Zw
> "Why OFB corporatisation is a bold Modi govt reform, key to India's Revolution in Military Affairs", 30 Sept 2021
> Remember defence sector also a very hi-tech sector.
>
> Also read up about the 40 defence labs under DRDO and of course ISRO. You will know the entire technical side of the defence industry.

**BEL** – Govt of India's recommended partner for tech transfer from MNCs, they maintain MNC defence equipment in India after the latter stop doing it, in some years they had negative working capital (meaning I think they got advance money from the client for supply of products). Interestingly HAL, BEL are pass through businesses,

---

[Page 2]

which means any expenses they incur are passed on to the client (Navy, Army..), so their businesses are bound to be profitable (thanks for Aatma Nirbhar Bharat).

**Astral poly** – is a market leader in CPVC (chlorinated polyvinyl chloride pipes) pipes with 25% market share in plumbing and drainage sectors [https://www.forbesindia.com/article/real-issue/how-astral-pipes-sandeep-engineer-became-a-mintnew-billionaire/52953/1].

**Cummins** – how does it sell at a premium compared to other engines? Find out!

**Asian Energy** – a zero debt company, which used to do mining surveys, today diversified into surveying for coal, oil and so on. Future looks interesting.

**NOCIL** - The largest rubber chemical manufacturing company in India. The twists and turns in its history are fascinating. Check out!

**CDSL** – It took 15 years to add 1 crore demat customers. The next 1 crore got added in a year. The next one crore got added in 2 months. Imagine, as India gets more and more financialized and formalized how big it can get.

**Indiamart** – there are 6.5 crore MSMEs in India. Of these only 20000 to 30000 are on an online platform. Eventually even if 20% of all the MSMEs get on to this platform think how strong this brand can get. (But is this threatened with the entry of JDMart of Reliance? Dinesh Agarwal the boss Indiamart doesn't think so. He says INdiamart is b2b, industrial and raw material supplier. While Udaan is more fmcg supplier consolidator (?) Not many customers are switching between us and Udaan [https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z3-WNzqZqbQ, Deep Dive Into Indiamart Intermesh & Swotlight On Glenmark Life Sciences | Inside Out | CNBC-TV18, 1,083 views, 2 Apr 2022, 9:30 to 11:30 am])

**Ion Exchange** (water purification) – has been performing very well for the last 4 years, check out why?

**MTAR** – a company that does cutting edge work for Nuclear Fuel Complex, BARC, ISRO. Got listed recently.

**Teamlease** – it is a company that helps in staffing, recruiting etc. Its founder Manish Sabharwal's views are often sought for understanding employment problems in India. He and CMIE are 2 sources that tell us how the job market works in India. (One must see video of his for all MBA students is "Why is India Poor? Manish Sabharwal talks at Manthan")

**Fiem industries** – they are in auto lighting, they are helping auto companies move to LED lighting, that is a big market, small but interesting company, reducing its debt, great traction in future.

**Lumax** – 60% share in automobile lighting in India

**Gabriel springs** – leading shock absorber and front fork manufacturers for 2 wheeler and 4 wheelers. It has 25 percent market share in 2W segment, 65 percent in 3Ws

---

[Page 3]

segment, 25 percent in passenger vehicles (PVs) and 85 percent in commercial vehicles (CVs).

**Sona Koyo** – a Deming Prize winner for quality that makes automobile steerings. The other two well known names that won the coveted quality award are Sundaram Clayton and Sundaram Fasteners.

**Harita** – makes seats for automobiles that get a premium.

**Subros** – a leading automobile a/c manufacturer in India in which Suzuki holds a stake. They have 40% market share in Passenger Car a/c and 60% Truck a/c.

**Bosch** – leading German auto component multinational particularly good at embedded controls for automobiles. Interestingly it is owned by a charitable institution by the same name.

**Crompton Greaves Power** – after going through several ups and downs, new management under Murugappa group turned it around, reducing its debt, paving way for a great future.

**Blue Dart** – well-run company, steadily reducing debt, charges a premium compared to competitors (check how they do it), unlike smaller companies managed Covid well through minimal touch delivery.

**Endurance technologies** – country's biggest aluminum casting company.

**Essel Propack** – Global leader that supplies soft squeeze tubes (e.g. your toothpaste tube) and a leading supplier to P&G and Unilever.

**ISGC Heavy** – initially into sugar plants and now diversified into several sectors (iron castings, presses, boilers, air pollution equipment) and countries. Interesting company.

**Motherson Sumi** – biggest wire harness manufacturer in India for cars, headwinds are chip shortage for car companies hurting it and slowing its harness consumption, raw material prices have gone up in the recent past.

**Garware technical fibre** – global leader in fishing net fibre manufacturer

**Divis Labs, Dr Reddy Labs, Lupin Labs, Cipla, Ranbaxy, Sun pharma** – all worth studying. Cipla is particularly good in "nasal" and has a better India footprint than competitors.

**Specialty chemicals** - **Navin Flourine** – chlorine in all industrial applications will probably be substituted by fluorine in future. Looks promising, therefore. **Alkyl amine, Balaji Amines, GACL, Aarti, Fine organics** – all specialty chemical companies that have a great future bcos the entire industry is shifting to India. Specialty chemicals is also a big domestic opportunity. Btw, it is difficult to believe that there are 11 application segments in specialty chemicals, a market space that we rarely bother to look at (Yet people like Nischal Maheswari of Edelweiss have been tracking this

---

[Page 4]

market since 2013. He was probably one of the earliest to spot the long-term shift of the business to India). The companies big in some of the segments are listed here (Agro-chem – PI industries, Surfactants – Galaxy surfactants, Polymers, Textiles – DCW, Dyes – Deepak Nitrite, Printing ink, Water management chemicals, Cosmetics, Adhesives – Pidilite, Flavors and fragrances - Bush, Boake, Allen, Food additives)

**Tata steel** (cheapest steel maker in the world probably)

**JSPL** – serious reduction in debt bcos it is selling power business

**Kanchi karpuram** – camphor making firm, interesting

**Tata power** – reducing debt, becoming a renewable power company, future looks bright

**L&T** – new businesses like IT, financial services and defence applications are their big bet for future. A professional company in which an engineer can become a Chairman.

**BHEL** – great order book, problems in land acquisition, execution, diversification into solar power, renewables, will they be able to fight Chinese and other competition in future?

**Concor** – a big player in multi-modal logistics. Sustainable advantages, it very difficult to build a business like Concor even if any private player invests for 12 years in it.

**KPIT** – IT services company with specific focus on auto sector

**Rivigo** – asset heavy Uber for lorries

**Hindalco** – Indian leader in aluminium, completely integrated from bauxite to value added products, big global acquisitions like Novellis, though there are concerns of debt.

**Amber** – big contract manufacturers for A/C systems and components like heat exchangers, motors etc.

**Dixon** – the ultimate OEM supplier, has 40% capacity of LED lighting in the country, expanding TV production to 40% of total, presence in mobiles market, washing machines market already has a tie-up with Bosch as anchor customer

**Ultratech** – biggest cement maker in the country with multiple plants in multiple locations, grows typically like the parent group, K M Birla, through acquisitions

**Bharat Forge** – one of the global leaders in forgings

**Coal India** – owns 80% of the coal mines in the country

---

[Page 5]

**Balmer Lawrie** – makes lubricants and oil drums, did not make a loss for 144 years (till about 4 years ago), but never made enough profit either — makes it interesting, therefore.

**MRF** - conservative management, dynamic brand, interesting how they are managing the duality and yet delivering great results

**Apollo Tyres** – Aggressive with global ambitions

**NBCC** – government consultant for many construction projects

**EIL** – public sector engineering equivalent of TCS

**Kansai Nerolac** – leader in automotive painting

**GMM Pfaudler** – global leader in glass lined vessels for chemical reactions

**Devyani International** – Largest franchisee of KFC and Pizza Hut in India. competitor to Jubilant (master franchisee of Domino's Pizza, Dunkin Donuts and Popeyes). McDonald's franchisee is Westlife and Connaught place restaurants (?).

> **Other interesting companies (mixed font/colour in original indicating faculty emphasis):**
>
> **RIL** (just the refinery business – for details see the book "Ambani and Sons" by Hamish McDonald), **BPCL** (refinery cluster to be privatized, check out their "Beyond the LPG" program), **GE** (excellent localization and "reverse innovation" [see Vijay Govindarajan for details]; check out their low cost versions of X-ray scanners, MRI m/cs, do-it-yourself ECGs costing Rs 9000 – excellent India specific innovation), **French major Areva** (capable of delivering nuclear power stations like Toshiba and Hitachi), **ABB** (leader in transformers, recent tech development – invented a process whereby a bus can get a top up battery charge rapidly in 17 sec), **Siemens** (a near 100 year old business in India, well known for a range of b2b products from switchgears to process controls), **Honeywell** (a company that saw 10 years of consistent growth in India, check why), the last mentioned three companies are listed in India. So are Pfizer and Glaxo global pharma majors)

## [PROFESSOR EXAM GUIDANCE]
Source: knowledge_base/reading_materials/how_to_answer_quizzes.md
---
# How to Answer Quizzes and Make Presentations

**Title:** How to Write Quizzes / How to Make Presentations
**Author(s):** Prof Y L R Moorthi (implied; internal course guidance note)
**Publication:** Course guidance note for Brand Management
**Year:** Not dated
**Original Filename:** how to answer quizs, make presentations.pdf

---

[Page 1]

## How to write quizs

A student often has a question "What is a good answer? What is a bad answer? How do I know? How do I know my answer is a loser?

Ask yourself "Is your answer likely to look like your neighbor's?". Then, in all probability, both of you will lose marks. The more the number of people that write an answer, the less credit the answer gets.

There are, of course, standard excuses. "We prepared together, so our answers are similar". That is a lot of baloney! If a group of 4 study together, why don't you think of 4 illustrations for the same concept? Then all of you will benefit from brain storming.

In short, show novelty in your answers. That is the surest way to score. Ideally no two answers in the class should look alike.

Just to make sure you understand, let me also show you **some bad answers for quiz questions.**

**Q1)** What are the limitations of marketing mix? (let us say this is the question).

**Silly ans 1** - Give weightages for the items in this conceptual framework.

*[The original document shows a diagram of the Marketing Mix framework with "Marketing Mix" at the top, connected to four sub-elements: Product (product variety, quality, design, features, brand name, packaging, sizes, services, warranties, returns), Price (list price, discounts, allowances, payment period, credit terms), Place (channels, coverage, assortments, locations, inventory, transport), and Promotion (sales promotion, advertising, sales force, public relations, direct marketing), with "Target Market" at the centre.]*

**Comment 1** - See the above framework below. What the answer is saying is that each of the elements under 4Ps (e.g. – under Product we have elements like product variety, quality, design, features etc. Similarly, under Price we have list price, discounts, allowances and so on. The answer proposes that each of the elements be given numerical weightages. Then it is more rigorous/useful).

---

[Page 2]

This is honestly a terrible answer (even if one wants to be charitable to student responses). How many theoretical frameworks have seen like balanced score card or Porter's 5 forces? How many of them have weightages? They cannot have weightages precisely because they are general purpose frameworks. The weightages depend on the product category, right? If the product is steel, the elements under the 4Ps will acquire certain weights, if it is cola then weights will be different and so on. This becomes obvious when we think.

**Q2)** Give an example of a cultural convention?

**Silly ans 2** - 1/4th of the class could think of only McDonalds not using beef filling in India as an example of cultural convention.

**Comment 2** – it is obvious that they copied from one another. If not that, then the excuse is we prepared together (I already mentioned how that can be overcome). There are hundred and twenty languages in this country, countless dialects, 29 States. All our friends could think of was beef in the burger. For instance, for a festival called Pola in Maharastra they color the horns of bulls. The same is done for Maattu Pongal in Tamil Nadu and Kanumu in AP/Telangana (this is the 3rd day of Pongal/Sankranti, usually 15 Jan). This cultural convention offers an interesting opportunity for paints companies to sell their paint. One is looking for answers like this.

**Q3)** Give an eg of an innovative campaign on social media?

**Silly ans 3** – 1/3rd of class could only think of Google Doodle.

**Comment 3** - Meaning 25 guys in the class couldn't think of anything else in social media. There are a thousand stories that went viral on Whatsapp. Don't they know even one? Such poverty of preparation and imagination!

**Q4)** Give an innovative thing you learnt from the article?

**Silly ans 4** - At least 20 people wrote M-Pesa.

**Comment 4** – the answer was in reference to a specific article I gave for quiz reading. This was an omnibus article penned by veterans like Rajan Varadarajan, V Kumar etc. They explained what matters for retailing in the developed and developing countries. Though the answer was quoted from the article it was a lazy answer bcos it was dated. Strangely, not even one student wrote the other e.g.s cited in the same article. For instance, Xidan a Chinese retail chain (if I remember), has products displayed on different floors of a building. The prices of products go up as you go up the floors. The retailer therefore, has smartly conveyed to the customer that if you take the elevator, you pay elevated prices. Fast selling, a garments company sells low priced stuff. They therefore used Grameen Bank customers to sell their wares. Again, this reveals smart thinking. Micro finance customers are usually

---

[Page 3]

looking for additional income sources. Also, they live in localities where people buy affordable products. They are an obvious channel for anybody who wishes to distribute economy ware. The interesting thing is these egs were given in the same article. It was somewhat intriguing that not even one student cited either example.

I hope I have been able to show you how and why students loose credit for their answers. Often it is just lack of preparation and lazy thinking. It can be easily remedied.

### Three more notes of caution on quizs

> **Note 1** (in red in original) - You cannot repeat the examples given by other presenting groups, illustrations discussed in class or examples given by faculty in quizs or presentations. Quiz answers must be your examples. You are expected to read up business press and get interesting info. Remember, this is an exercise to test your originality not your memorizing capability.

> **Note 2** (in red in original) – All egs should relate to Indian market. Do not give egs of US or Europe. You can however cite illustrations of Walmart or Caterpillar in India (not Wal mart of Cat in US). Or you can cite Indian brands like Mother's Diary and Infosys. In short you can give illustrations of MNCs or Indian Co.s wrt their Indian marketing operations.

> **Note 3** (in red in original) - Two e.g.s are banned in all BM quizs, namely Patanjali and Apple. These two have become stock answers for all marketing questions, hence banned. You will get negative marks if I see Patanjali or Apple in your quiz answers.

### Presentations

What are bad presentations?

Presentations that have motherhood, twenty thousand feet statements. A typical e.g. of such a statement is say "Dabur should be innovative". This is nonsense. To put it in the lingo you understand, this is GLOBE!

So, when is something GLOBE?

Consider the statement - "Dabur should be innovative". In this answer, the name "Dabur" can be substituted by any other company like HP, Microsoft, Mahindra tractors, Athica or even your mess. This is smoke-and-mirrors! Your answer is supposed to tell how exactly Dabur should be innovative. An interesting answer is, say, "branding neem sticks". To the extent I know, no FMCG company has branded neem sticks in India. Both in urban and rural India this product can click. Bcos urban Indians are looking for "green" products. Rural folks use neem sticks anyway for brushing.

---

[Page 4]

So also consider the statement - Whirlpool should be innovative. Here also the expectation is you write how exactly Whirlpool can become innovative. For instance, Whirlpool can launch washing m/cs that understand voice commands in Indian languages. That sure sounds like innovation.

Look at this answer - Marico should be innovative. Sure, but how exactly? For instance, by offering hair oil with customizable perfume.

Etc….etc….

This is how you make your answer interesting/original. In fact, the expectation is even less. The expectation is that you just read real life examples of innovation in marketing about brands in the Indian market and cite them in your presentations and quizs. (in red in original) That will more or less see you through.

I hope you do not feel I am rubbing this in. If I do not send this approach note, I feared, I might have a repeat of what I witnessed year after year, in my long tryst with teaching. I do hope that this helps you prepare for your presentations and quizs.

All the very best!
